{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Wb3jHTvj7xcmyNTjRscNo7","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→title: \"sc:cli-portify Workflow Evolution — Replace Code Generation with Spec-Driven Planning\"\n     3→version: \"1.1.0\"\n     4→status: reviewed\n     5→feature_id: FR-060\n     6→parent_feature: cli-portify-protocol\n     7→spec_type: refactoring\n     8→complexity_score: 0.60\n     9→complexity_class: moderate\n    10→target_release: v2.20\n    11→authors: [user, claude]\n    12→created: 2026-03-09\n    13→---\n    14→\n    15→# FR-060: sc:cli-portify Workflow Evolution\n    16→\n    17→## 1. Problem Statement\n    18→\n    19→The current `sc:cli-portify` protocol attempts to one-shot complex code generation across 12+ interdependent Python files (Phase 3) and wire them into the CLI infrastructure (Phase 4) based solely on a pipeline specification. This approach:\n    20→\n    21→1. **Bypasses the project's own planning infrastructure** — does not use `sc:brainstorm` for gap analysis, `sc:spec-panel` for expert review, or `sc:roadmap` for milestone planning\n    22→2. **Is high-risk one-shot execution** — generating 12+ files with cross-file dependencies from templates has no incremental validation or recovery loop\n    23→3. **Produces the wrong deliverable** — outputs code directly instead of a reviewed specification that feeds the existing planning → implementation pipeline\n    24→4. **Lacks specification quality validation** — no expert panel review before committing to code generation, missing the gap/edge-case analysis that brainstorm and spec-panel provide\n    25→\n    26→### 1.1 Evidence\n    27→\n    28→| Evidence | Source | Impact |\n    29→|----------|--------|--------|\n    30→| Forensic analysis identifies seam failures as primary failure habitat | `forensic-foundation-validated.md` F-006 | Spec→code is the highest-risk seam; skipping spec review amplifies this |\n    31→| \"Structural validation is systematically mistaken for semantic correctness\" | `forensic-foundation-validated.md` F-001 | Template-based code generation validates structure but not semantic correctness |\n    32→| Phase 3 generates 12+ files with no incremental gate between files | `refactoring-spec-cli-portify.md` §2.4 | Single failure mid-generation can leave inconsistent partial output |\n    33→| No standardized spec template exists for release specifications | Backlog v4.0 research | Each spec uses ad-hoc structure, making quality inconsistent |\n    34→\n    35→### 1.2 Scope Boundary\n    36→\n    37→**In scope**:\n    38→- Replace Phase 3 (Code Generation) and Phase 4 (Integration) with spec synthesis + review phases\n    39→- Create a general-purpose release spec template\n    40→- Integrate automated brainstorm (multi-persona gap analysis) into the workflow\n    41→- Integrate spec-panel review (two passes: focus + critique) into the workflow\n    42→- Update the protocol skill, refs, and command shim accordingly\n    43→\n    44→**Out of scope**:\n    45→- Modifying Phase 0 (Prerequisites), Phase 1 (Workflow Analysis), or Phase 2 (Pipeline Specification)\n    46→- Implementing the full v4.0 Spec Generator Framework\n    47→- Changes to `sc:brainstorm` or `sc:spec-panel` command definitions\n    48→- Changes to the pipeline/ or sprint/ infrastructure modules\n    49→- Building a replacement code generation system\n    50→\n    51→## 2. Solution Overview\n    52→\n    53→Replace the code generation phases with a spec-driven planning pipeline that produces a reviewed release specification as its deliverable. The spec is then consumed by a human → `sc:roadmap` → `sc:tasklist` → implementation workflow.\n    54→\n    55→### 2.1 Key Design Decisions\n    56→\n    57→| Decision | Choice | Alternatives Considered | Rationale |\n    58→|----------|--------|------------------------|-----------|\n    59→| Spec template scope | General-purpose release spec | Portify-specific template; Full v4.0 template system | Reusable across workflows without over-engineering; v4.0 is future work |\n    60→| Brainstorm integration | Embedded multi-persona behavioral patterns (Option C) | Interactive Socratic dialogue; Guided self-review; Direct sc:brainstorm invocation | Non-interactive keeps the pipeline automatable; embedding avoids fragile inter-skill coupling |\n    61→| Spec panel configuration | Convergent loop: focus+critique with max 3 iterations | Single-pass critique; Two-pass without loop; User-configurable per invocation | Convergence guarantees NFR-060.5 compliance; additive-only constraint prevents introduction of new issues |\n    62→| Code generation fate | Removed entirely | Move to separate command; Keep as optional Phase | Clean separation of planning from execution; the roadmap→implement path handles it |\n    63→| `--dry-run` behavior | Keep same (Phases 0-2 only) | Extend to include spec synthesis | Consistent with current behavior; user already expects analysis-only output |\n    64→| Template location | `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md` | In skill templates/; In shared templates/ | Examples directory is the canonical location for reusable reference files |\n    65→| Placeholder sentinel | `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:name}}` | `{PLACEHOLDER}`; `__PLACEHOLDER__` | Unique sentinel avoids collision with legitimate template content in specs about templates |\n    66→| Quality score formula | `overall = mean(clarity, completeness, testability, consistency)` | Weighted average; Minimum of dimensions | Simple arithmetic mean is transparent and auditable; no dimension is structurally more important |\n    67→| CRITICAL finding disposition | Incorporate OR justify-dismiss (both count as \"addressed\") | Must incorporate (no dismissal); User override only | Allows handling false positives without bypassing quality gates |\n    68→| Incorporation constraint | Additive-only (append/extend, no rewrites) | Full rewrite allowed; Conservative rewrite | Prevents incorporation from introducing new issues that trigger convergence loops |\n    69→\n    70→### 2.2 Workflow / Data Flow\n    71→\n    72→**Current (v2.18)**:\n    73→```\n    74→Phase 0: Prerequisites → api-snapshot.yaml\n    75→    ↓\n    76→Phase 1: Workflow Analysis → portify-analysis.md + .yaml\n    77→    ↓ (user review)\n    78→Phase 2: Pipeline Specification → portify-spec.md + .yaml\n    79→    ↓ (user approval)\n    80→Phase 3: Code Generation → 12+ Python files         ← REMOVED\n    81→    ↓\n    82→Phase 4: Integration → main.py patch, tests, summary  ← REMOVED\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→**Proposed (v2.20)**:\n    86→```\n    87→Phase 0: Prerequisites → api-snapshot.yaml                [UNCHANGED]\n    88→    ↓\n    89→Phase 1: Workflow Analysis → portify-analysis.md + .yaml  [UNCHANGED]\n    90→    ↓ (user review)\n    91→Phase 2: Pipeline Specification → portify-spec.md + .yaml [UNCHANGED]\n    92→    ↓ (user approval)\n    93→Phase 3: Release Spec Synthesis                            [NEW]\n    94→    ├─ 3a: Template instantiation from release-spec-template.md\n    95→    ├─ 3b: Populate from Phase 1 analysis + Phase 2 spec\n    96→    ├─ 3c: Automated brainstorm (multi-persona gap analysis)\n    97→    └─ 3d: Incorporate brainstorm findings into spec\n    98→    → portify-release-spec.md (draft)\n    99→    ↓ \"sc:cli-portify Workflow Evolution — Replace Code Generation with Spec-Driven Planning\"\nversion: \"1.1.0\"\nstatus: reviewed\nfeature_id: FR-060\nparent_feature: cli-portify-protocol\nspec_type: refactoring\ncomplexity_score: 0.60\ncomplexity_class: moderate\ntarget_release: v2.20\nauthors: [user, claude]\ncreated: 2026-03-09\n---\n\n# FR-060: sc:cli-portify Workflow Evolution\n\n## 1. Problem Statement\n\nThe current `sc:cli-portify` protocol attempts to one-shot complex code generation across 12+ interdependent Python files (Phase 3) and wire them into the CLI infrastructure (Phase 4) based solely on a pipeline specification. This approach:\n\n1. **Bypasses the project's own planning infrastructure** — does not use `sc:brainstorm` for gap analysis, `sc:spec-panel` for expert review, or `sc:roadmap` for milestone planning\n2. **Is high-risk one-shot execution** — generating 12+ files with cross-file dependencies from templates has no incremental validation or recovery loop\n3. **Produces the wrong deliverable** — outputs code directly instead of a reviewed specification that feeds the existing planning → implementation pipeline\n4. **Lacks specification quality validation** — no expert panel review before committing to code generation, missing the gap/edge-case analysis that brainstorm and spec-panel provide\n\n### 1.1 Evidence\n\n| Evidence | Source | Impact |\n|----------|--------|--------|\n| Forensic analysis identifies seam failures as primary failure habitat | `forensic-foundation-validated.md` F-006 | Spec→code is the highest-risk seam; skipping spec review amplifies this |\n| \"Structural validation is systematically mistaken for semantic correctness\" | `forensic-foundation-validated.md` F-001 | Template-based code generation validates structure but not semantic correctness |\n| Phase 3 generates 12+ files with no incremental gate between files | `refactoring-spec-cli-portify.md` §2.4 | Single failure mid-generation can leave inconsistent partial output |\n| No standardized spec template exists for release specifications | Backlog v4.0 research | Each spec uses ad-hoc structure, making quality inconsistent |\n\n### 1.2 Scope Boundary\n\n**In scope**:\n- Replace Phase 3 (Code Generation) and Phase 4 (Integration) with spec synthesis + review phases\n- Create a general-purpose release spec template\n- Integrate automated brainstorm (multi-persona gap analysis) into the workflow\n- Integrate spec-panel review (two passes: focus + critique) into the workflow\n- Update the protocol skill, refs, and command shim accordingly\n\n**Out of scope**:\n- Modifying Phase 0 (Prerequisites), Phase 1 (Workflow Analysis), or Phase 2 (Pipeline Specification)\n- Implementing the full v4.0 Spec Generator Framework\n- Changes to `sc:brainstorm` or `sc:spec-panel` command definitions\n- Changes to the pipeline/ or sprint/ infrastructure modules\n- Building a replacement code generation system\n\n## 2. Solution Overview\n\nReplace the code generation phases with a spec-driven planning pipeline that produces a reviewed release specification as its deliverable. The spec is then consumed by a human → `sc:roadmap` → `sc:tasklist` → implementation workflow.\n\n### 2.1 Key Design Decisions\n\n| Decision | Choice | Alternatives Considered | Rationale |\n|----------|--------|------------------------|-----------|\n| Spec template scope | General-purpose release spec | Portify-specific template; Full v4.0 template system | Reusable across workflows without over-engineering; v4.0 is future work |\n| Brainstorm integration | Embedded multi-persona behavioral patterns (Option C) | Interactive Socratic dialogue; Guided self-review; Direct sc:brainstorm invocation | Non-interactive keeps the pipeline automatable; embedding avoids fragile inter-skill coupling |\n| Spec panel configuration | Convergent loop: focus+critique with max 3 iterations | Single-pass critique; Two-pass without loop; User-configurable per invocation | Convergence guarantees NFR-060.5 compliance; additive-only constraint prevents introduction of new issues |\n| Code generation fate | Removed entirely | Move to separate command; Keep as optional Phase | Clean separation of planning from execution; the roadmap→implement path handles it |\n| `--dry-run` behavior | Keep same (Phases 0-2 only) | Extend to include spec synthesis | Consistent with current behavior; user already expects analysis-only output |\n| Template location | `src/superclaude/examples/release-spec-template.md` | In skill templates/; In shared templates/ | Examples directory is the canonical location for reusable reference files |\n| Placeholder sentinel | `{{SC_PLACEHOLDER:name}}` | `{PLACEHOLDER}`; `__PLACEHOLDER__` | Unique sentinel avoids collision with legitimate template content in specs about templates |\n| Quality score formula | `overall = mean(clarity, completeness, testability, consistency)` | Weighted average; Minimum of dimensions | Simple arithmetic mean is transparent and auditable; no dimension is structurally more important |\n| CRITICAL finding disposition | Incorporate OR justify-dismiss (both count as \"addressed\") | Must incorporate (no dismissal); User override only | Allows handling false positives without bypassing quality gates |\n| Incorporation constraint | Additive-only (append/extend, no rewrites) | Full rewrite allowed; Conservative rewrite | Prevents incorporation from introducing new issues that trigger convergence loops |\n\n### 2.2 Workflow / Data Flow\n\n**Current (v2.18)**:\n```\nPhase 0: Prerequisites → api-snapshot.yaml\n    ↓\nPhase 1: Workflow Analysis → portify-analysis.md + .yaml\n    ↓ (user review)\nPhase 2: Pipeline Specification → portify-spec.md + .yaml\n    ↓ (user approval)\nPhase 3: Code Generation → 12+ Python files         ← REMOVED\n    ↓\nPhase 4: Integration → main.py patch, tests, summary  ← REMOVED\n```\n\n**Proposed (v2.20)**:\n```\nPhase 0: Prerequisites → api-snapshot.yaml                [UNCHANGED]\n    ↓\nPhase 1: Workflow Analysis → portify-analysis.md + .yaml  [UNCHANGED]\n    ↓ (user review)\nPhase 2: Pipeline Specification → portify-spec.md + .yaml [UNCHANGED]\n    ↓ (user approval)\nPhase 3: Release Spec Synthesis                            [NEW]\n    ├─ 3a: Template instantiation from release-spec-template.md\n    ├─ 3b: Populate from Phase 1 analysis + Phase 2 spec\n    ├─ 3c: Automated brainstorm (multi-persona gap analysis)\n    └─ 3d: Incorporate brainstorm findings into spec\n    → portify-release-spec.md (draft)\n    ↓ (automatic)\nPhase 4: Spec Panel Review (Convergent Loop)                [NEW]","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":789}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01DcmeLyBavMrt9rKUwETBRG","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→---\n     2→name: sc-cli-portify-protocol\n     3→description: \"Full behavioral protocol for sc:cli-portify — port inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines with sprint-style supervised execution.\"\n     4→category: development\n     5→complexity: high\n     6→allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task\n     7→mcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]\n     8→personas: [architect, analyzer, backend]\n     9→argument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\"\n    10→---\n    11→\n    12→# sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler\n    13→\n    14→Convert inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines that ensure 100% completion and consistency between runs.\n    15→\n    16→## Purpose\n    17→\n    18→SuperClaude workflows implemented as commands + skills + agents + refs rely entirely on Claude's reasoning for orchestration. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n    19→\n    20→- **Deterministic control flow** — Python decides what runs when, not inference\n    21→- **Formal artifact validation** — Gates check output quality programmatically\n    22→- **Resume/retry** — Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n    23→- **Live monitoring** — TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n    24→- **Budget economics** — Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n    25→- **Consistent behavior** — Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n    26→\n    27→The existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n    28→\n    29→## What Gets Generated\n    30→\n    31→A CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n    32→\n    33→| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n    34→|------|---------|----------------|\n    35→| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n    36→| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n    37→| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n    38→| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n    39→| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n    40→| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n    41→| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n    42→| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n    43→| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n    44→| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n    45→| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n    46→| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n    47→| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n    48→| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n    49→\n    50→Plus integration patches for `main.py`.\n    51→\n    52→## Required Input\n    53→\n    54→```\n    55→/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n    56→```\n    57→\n    58→| Argument | Required | Description |\n    59→|----------|----------|-------------|\n    60→| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n    61→| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n    62→| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n    63→| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating code |\n    64→| `--skip-integration` | No | Generate module only, skip main.py wiring |\n    65→\n    66→**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n    67→\n    68→## Behavioral Flow\n    69→\n    70→Four phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n    71→\n    72→### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n    73→\n    74→Load `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n    75→\n    76→**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n    77→\n    78→1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n    79→\n    80→2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n    81→   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n    82→   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n    83→   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n    84→   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n    85→\n    86→3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n    87→   - A new artifact is produced\n    88→   - A different agent takes over\n    89→   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n    90→   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n    91→   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n    92→\n    93→4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n    94→   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n    95→   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n    96→   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n    97→\n    98→5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n    99→\n   100→6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n   101→\n   102→7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n   103→\n   104→**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n   105→\n   106→**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n   107→\n   108→### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n   109→\n   110→Load `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n   111→\n   112→**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n   113→\n   114→1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n   115→\n   116→2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   117→   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   118→   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   119→   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   120→   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   121→   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   122→   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n   123→\n   124→3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   125→   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   126→   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   127→   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   128→   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n   129→\n   130→   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n   131→\n   132→4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   133→   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   134→   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   135→   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n   136→\n   137→5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n   138→\n   139→6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   140→   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   141→   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   142→   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   143→   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   144→   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   145→   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   146→   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   147→   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n   148→\n   149→7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n   150→\n   151→**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n   152→\n   153→**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n   154→\n   155→### Phase 3: Code Generation\n   156→\n   157→Load `refs/code-templates.md` before this phase. It contains parameterized file templates for every module.\n   158→\n   159→Generate files in dependency order (models → gates → prompts → config → monitor → process → executor → tui → logging → diagnostics → commands → __init__). Each file imports from `superclaude.cli.pipeline` for shared base types and follows sprint/roadmap naming conventions.\n   160→\n   161→### Phase 4: Integration\n   162→\n   163→1. Patch `main.py` — Add import and `app.add_command()`\n   164→2. Verify imports — Quick check for circular dependencies\n   165→3. Generate structural test — Validates step graph, gate definitions, and model consistency\n   166→4. Write `portify-summary.md` — File inventory, CLI usage, step graph, known limitations\n   167→\n   168→## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n   169→\n   170→The value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n   171→\n   172→| Operation | Classification | Why |\n   173→|-----------|---------------|-----|\n   174→| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n   175→| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n   176→| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n   177→| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n   178→| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n   179→| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n   180→| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n   181→| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n   182→| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n   183→| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n   184→| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n   185→\n   186→### Rule of Thumb\n   187→If you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. If it requires reading natural language, making judgments, or synthesizing information, use Claude with a gate to verify the output.\n   188→\n   189→## Code Generation Principles\n   190→\n   191→These align with the unified-audit-gating architecture in `pipeline/`.\n   192→\n   193→### Critical Constraints\n   194→1. **Synchronous execution** — Sprint uses `threading` + `time.sleep()` polling. Use `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism. Do NOT use async/await.\n   195→2. **Gate function signatures** — All semantic checks return `tuple[bool, str]`. The reason string feeds diagnostics and retry decisions.\n   196→3. **Runner-authored truth** — Reports derive from runner-observed data (exit codes, artifacts, gates, monitor signals), not Claude's self-reported status.\n   197→4. **Deterministic flow control** — Python makes all decisions about what runs next. Claude never decides \"what's next\".\n   198→\n   199→### Shared Pipeline Patterns\n   200→5. **Reuse `pipeline/` primitives** — `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult`, `GateMode`, `GateCriteria`, `SemanticCheck`, `gate_passed()`, `ClaudeProcess`\n   201→6. **Gate modes** — `BLOCKING` (default) stops pipeline on failure. `TRAILING` defers evaluation. Use trailing only for quality checks that don't affect downstream data flow.\n   202→7. **Turn budget** — `TurnLedger` with debit/credit/guard for multi-subprocess pipelines. Pre-launch guards prevent launching when budget too low.\n   203→8. **Subprocess isolation** — 4-layer model: scoped work dir, git ceiling, isolated plugin dir, isolated settings dir.\n   204→9. **Context injection** — Prior results serialized into subsequent prompts. Compress older, preserve recent.\n   205→10. **Resume-first failures** — On halt: exact resume command, remaining work, diagnostic path, budget suggestion.\n   206→11. **Diagnostic chain** — Runner-side failure analysis that doesn't consume turn budget.\n   207→\n   208→### Output Guidance\n   209→- `portify-analysis.md`: Under 400 lines. Step graph, gates, data flow.\n   210→- `portify-spec.md`: Split prompts to separate file if spec exceeds 800 lines.\n   211→- Pure-programmatic steps: Full implementation code, not descriptions.\n   212→\n   213→## Boundaries\n   214→\n   215→### Will Do\n   216→- Analyze any SuperClaude skill/command/agent workflow\n   217→- Decompose into structured pipeline specification\n   218→- Generate sc-cli-portify-protocol\ndescription: \"Full behavioral protocol for sc:cli-portify — port inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines with sprint-style supervised execution.\"\ncategory: development\ncomplexity: high\nallowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Edit, Write, Bash, TodoWrite, Task\nmcp-servers: [sequential, serena, context7, auggie-mcp]\npersonas: [architect, analyzer, backend]\nargument-hint: \"--workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>] [--dry-run] [--skip-integration]\"\n---\n\n# sc:cli-portify — Workflow-to-CLI Pipeline Compiler\n\nConvert inference-based SuperClaude workflows into programmatic CLI pipelines that ensure 100% completion and consistency between runs.\n\n## Purpose\n\nSuperClaude workflows implemented as commands + skills + agents + refs rely entirely on Claude's reasoning for orchestration. This works well for flexible, one-off tasks but breaks down for repeatable multi-step pipelines where you need:\n\n- **Deterministic control flow** — Python decides what runs when, not inference\n- **Formal artifact validation** — Gates check output quality programmatically\n- **Resume/retry** — Failed steps resume without re-running everything\n- **Live monitoring** — TUI shows progress, stall detection, diagnostics\n- **Budget economics** — Turn ledger tracks consumption across subprocesses\n- **Consistent behavior** — Same inputs produce structurally identical outputs every run\n\nThe existing `pipeline/` and `sprint/` modules already solve these problems. This skill bridges the gap by analyzing a workflow and generating a new CLI module that uses these proven patterns.\n\n## What Gets Generated\n\nA CLI subcommand package under `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`:\n\n| File | Purpose | When Generated |\n|------|---------|----------------|\n| `models.py` | Domain types extending `PipelineConfig`, `Step`, `StepResult` | Always |\n| `gates.py` | `GateCriteria` + semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]` | Always |\n| `prompts.py` | LLM contract builders per Claude-assisted step | Always |\n| `config.py` | CLI arg resolution, file discovery, config construction | Always |\n| `executor.py` | Synchronous supervisor loop with `ThreadPoolExecutor` for parallelism | Always |\n| `monitor.py` | NDJSON incremental output parser with domain signals | Always |\n| `process.py` | `ClaudeProcess` subclass with domain-specific prompt building | Always |\n| `tui.py` | Rich live dashboard with gate state machine | Always |\n| `logging_.py` | Dual JSONL + Markdown execution logging | Always |\n| `diagnostics.py` | `DiagnosticCollector`, `FailureClassifier`, `ReportGenerator` | Always |\n| `commands.py` | Click CLI group and subcommands | Always |\n| `__init__.py` | Package exports | Always |\n| `inventory.py` | Pure-programmatic file discovery/classification | If workflow has discovery steps |\n| `filtering.py` | Pure-programmatic inter-step data filtering | If workflow has filtering between steps |\n\nPlus integration patches for `main.py`.\n\n## Required Input\n\n```\n/sc:cli-portify --workflow <skill-name-or-path> [--name <cli-name>] [--output <dir>]\n```\n\n| Argument | Required | Description |\n|----------|----------|-------------|\n| `--workflow` | Yes | Skill directory path or `sc-*` name to portify |\n| `--name` | No | CLI subcommand name (default: derived from workflow) |\n| `--output` | No | Output directory (default: `src/superclaude/cli/<name>/`) |\n| `--dry-run` | No | Show decomposition plan without generating code |\n| `--skip-integration` | No | Generate module only, skip main.py wiring |\n\n**STOP** if `--workflow` is not provided or the path doesn't resolve to a valid skill.\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\nFour phases, each producing artifacts that feed the next. Present output to user for review after Phases 1 and 2 before continuing.\n\n### Phase 1: Workflow Analysis\n\nLoad `refs/analysis-protocol.md` before this phase. It contains the discovery checklist, step decomposition algorithm, classification rubric, and output format template.\n\n**Goal**: Decompose the target workflow into a structured pipeline specification.\n\n1. **Discover components** — Find the command `.md`, skill `SKILL.md`, all `refs/` and `rules/`, all `templates/`, all `scripts/`, and all referenced agents. Build a component inventory table with paths, line counts, and purposes.\n\n2. **Map the protocol** — Extract the step-by-step behavioral flow. Pay attention to:\n   - Wave/phase boundaries in the skill\n   - Agent delegation patterns (which agent, parallel vs sequential)\n   - Conditional execution paths (flags that skip steps)\n   - Implicit inter-step data flow (what one step produces that another consumes)\n\n3. **Identify steps** — A new Step boundary exists when:\n   - A new artifact is produced\n   - A different agent takes over\n   - Execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n   - A quality gate must be evaluated\n   - Operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\n4. **Classify each step** on the programmatic spectrum:\n   - **Pure programmatic**: Runs as a Python function, no Claude subprocess. Examples: file inventory via `git ls-files`, config construction, file filtering between passes, scoring formulas, structural validation, batch assignment. If the logic is deterministic and the input/output formats are well-defined, it should be programmatic.\n   - **Claude-assisted**: Runs as a Claude subprocess with a prompt contract and gate. Examples: content analysis, writing reports, rubric-based assessment, creative synthesis, debate.\n   - **Hybrid**: Programmatic setup → Claude subprocess → programmatic validation. Examples: steps that need Claude for content but have strict structural validation on the output.\n\n5. **Map dependencies and parallel groups** — Draw the data flow: which steps produce artifacts consumed by downstream steps? Which steps are independent and can run concurrently? For batched workflows, identify where batch parallelism applies.\n\n6. **Extract gates** — For each step output, identify what validation the original workflow expects. Map these to gate tiers: EXEMPT (informational), LIGHT (exists + non-empty), STANDARD (structural checks), STRICT (structural + semantic).\n\n7. **Assign gate modes** — `GateMode.BLOCKING` for steps whose output feeds downstream steps. `GateMode.TRAILING` for quality-only checks that don't affect data flow.\n\n**Output**: `portify-analysis.md` — Complete decomposition following the template in `refs/analysis-protocol.md`. Must include: component inventory, step graph with classifications, parallel groups, gates summary, data flow diagram, and recommendations.\n\n**Present to user for review before Phase 2.**\n\n### Phase 2: Pipeline Specification\n\nLoad `refs/pipeline-spec.md` before this phase. It contains Step definition patterns, model design patterns, gate patterns, executor patterns, and the new unified-audit-gating patterns (TurnLedger, gate modes, subprocess isolation, context injection, resume semantics).\n\n**Goal**: Convert the analysis into concrete, code-ready specifications.\n\n1. **Design the Step graph** — Map each workflow step to `Step` objects. Batched parallel steps are `list[Step]` groups. Dynamic step counts (e.g., batch count determined at runtime) require a `build_steps()` function.\n\n2. **Define models** — Design domain-specific dataclasses:\n   - Config extending `PipelineConfig` with workflow-specific fields (source paths, pass selection, batch sizes, stall/timeout policies)\n   - Status enum with domain-specific states (e.g., `VALIDATION_FAIL`, `CRITICAL_FAIL` for audit workflows)\n   - Result extending `StepResult` with execution telemetry\n   - Aggregate result with `resume_command()` and `suggested_resume_budget`\n   - Monitor state with domain-specific NDJSON signals\n   - `TurnLedger` integration for budget tracking\n\n3. **Design prompts** — For each Claude-assisted step, write the prompt builder. Each prompt must specify:\n   - What input files/context to embed (inline for <50KB, `--file` args for larger)\n   - Required output sections and frontmatter fields\n   - Machine-readable markers: `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT`\n   - Any structural requirements the gate will check\n\n   If prompts collectively exceed ~300 lines, put them in a separate `portify-prompts.md`.\n\n4. **Design gates** — For each output artifact, define:\n   - `GateCriteria` with tier, required frontmatter, min lines, semantic checks\n   - `GateMode` (BLOCKING or TRAILING)\n   - All semantic check functions returning `tuple[bool, str]`\n\n5. **Implement pure-programmatic steps** — Write actual runnable Python code for steps classified as \"pure programmatic\". These run as direct function calls in the executor, bypassing `ClaudeProcess`. Include: file discovery, domain classification, batch assignment, inter-pass filtering, config construction.\n\n6. **Design the executor** — Sprint-style synchronous supervisor:\n   - `ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch parallelism (NOT async/await)\n   - `time.sleep()` polling loops for monitoring\n   - Per-step/batch monitoring with stall detection\n   - `TurnLedger` budget guards before each launch\n   - Runner-authored truth: reports from observed data, not Claude self-reporting\n   - Subprocess isolation (4-layer model) for child Claude sessions\n   - Context injection: prior results compressed into subsequent prompts\n   - Signal-aware shutdown with `SignalHandler`\n\n7. **Plan integration** — Click command group, main.py import, file generation order.\n\n**Output**: `portify-spec.md` (+ optional `portify-prompts.md`) — Complete code spec with models, gates, executor design, pure-programmatic implementations, and integration plan.\n\n**Present to user for approval before Phase 3.**\n\n### Phase 3: Code Generation\n\nLoad `refs/code-templates.md` before this phase. It contains parameterized file templates for every module.\n\nGenerate files in dependency order (models → gates → prompts → config → monitor → process → executor → tui → logging → diagnostics → commands → __init__). Each file imports from `superclaude.cli.pipeline` for shared base types and follows sprint/roadmap naming conventions.\n\n### Phase 4: Integration\n\n1. Patch `main.py` — Add import and `app.add_command()`\n2. Verify imports — Quick check for circular dependencies\n3. Generate structural test — Validates step graph, gate definitions, and model consistency\n4. Write `portify-summary.md` — File inventory, CLI usage, step graph, known limitations\n\n## Decision Framework: What Becomes Programmatic\n\nThe value of portification is moving orchestration out of inference. Here are concrete examples from tested workflows:\n\n| Operation | Classification | Why |\n|-----------|---------------|-----|\n| Enumerate repo files | Pure programmatic | `git ls-files` + pattern matching is deterministic |\n| Classify file domains | Pure programmatic | Extension/path pattern rules, no judgment needed |\n| Assign files to batches | Pure programmatic | Math: divide files by batch_size, assign to agents |\n| Filter Pass 1 results for Pass 2 | Pure programmatic | Parse markdown, extract classifications, filter list |\n| Analyze file for issues | Claude-assisted | Requires reading code, understanding context |\n| Score variant quality | Hybrid | Formulas are programmatic, rubric evaluation is Claude |\n| Validate structural integrity | Pure programmatic | Regex checks, section presence, field counts |\n| Spot-check verification | Claude-assisted | Re-reads files, re-evaluates claims independently |\n| Merge batch reports | Claude-assisted | Requires synthesis, deduplication, pattern extraction |\n| Compute convergence score | Pure programmatic | `agreed / total` — arithmetic |\n| Generate executive summary | Claude-assisted | Requires narrative synthesis |\n\n### Rule of Thumb\nIf you can write a Python function for it with clear input→output types and no ambiguity, make it programmatic. Problem Statement\n    28→\n    29→> What problem does this work solve? Why does it matter? What fails or is suboptimal today?\n    30→\n    31→{PROBLEM_DESCRIPTION}\n    32→\n    33→### 1.1 Evidence\n    34→\n    35→> Concrete evidence that the problem exists. Solution Overview\n    50→\n    51→> High-level description of the approach. What changes, what stays the same.\n    52→\n    53→{SOLUTION_OVERVIEW}\n    54→\n    55→### 2.1 Key Design Decisions\n    56→\n    57→> Decisions made during brainstorming/design that shaped this spec. Use ASCII diagrams for pipeline flows.\n    66→\n    67→```\n    68→{FLOW_DIAGRAM}\n    69→```\n    70→\n    71→## 3. Functional Requirements\n    72→\n    73→> Numbered requirements.
